It may work well on some other type of hair, but for baby-fine curls, this product is a disaster.

Its a bit thicker than shampoo, of course, and it will take some getting used to, but keep working at it<br />4. take as many pumps as you like to coat the ends of your hair. You will find as you get used to using this that when you do the final rinse, the product will run down into the ends of your hair cleaning and softening it, so this part you may not even want to do.<br />5. take a few minutes and get on with your shower, shave, etc....<br />6 after at least 3 minutes, add water to the scalp and hair, and continue to work it in a bit, (you will find this part easier than when you first applied it) then start to rinse.<br />7. Rinse throughly....rinse!!<br />8. Finish with a light conditioner if you wish. Fine haired, normal or un damaged textured people might skip this part all together....I personally use a light conditioner always.<br />9. Dry your hair and style<br />10. It does a great job of cleansing the hair and scalp without the harsh detergents found in shampoos, while also leaving hair soft and manageable. It is NOT a shampoo! It has the slightest but of lather, but not much. It's not supposed to. Lather is not indicitave of cleansing power. Don't worry, you'll get through the lather addiction with time. Stick with it. It's worth it! Again, this is not a shampoo, so if you use heavy product, especially products with silicone, it won't be able to dissolve the silicone. Go silicone-free, and this will work like a dream. Or, if you aren't ready to go completely shampoo- or silicone-free, use this in-between shampoos as a conditioner. It took me a while to get used to being shampoo-free. Stick with it!   304. This crÃ¨me cleanser is very effective with keeping my hair soft, shiny and manageable. It is not regular shampoo, so you might need some practice (like you would with Wen), in order to really use it the right way. I flip my head over and let the water run on the back of my head and really saturate my hair (I find this is the best way for me to use this product). Next, I put a few pumps (you will figure out how much you need eventually) in my hand and start with the first section (the front of my head). I gently massage the cleanser on my scalp until a low lather develops. Then I continue this method throughout my whole head. I also add a few splashes of water to create an effective lather. If you don't use enough water then it will not work correctly. After I have a nice low lather, I finger comb or use a wide tooth comb to distribute the product to the rest of my hair. Then I clip my hair up and let it sit while I wash my body. This type of cleanser does take work, but once you get the hang of it, you will be very satisfied with the results. I'm sure YouTube has instructional videos if you are unsure of how to apply the product. It is very similar to Wen, although I find that Wen is the best cleanser for hair EVER, although very expensive! This is a close second! I have long fine hair and a very oily scalp (I have to wash my hair everyday or else I have a grease slick!) and this product does not leave my hair greasy. My ends are dry too when I use traditional shampoos, but when I use this cleanser, my ends blow out so nice and my hair doesn't separate as much or look straggly. Enjoy!
